<p><b>Victor Emmanuel III</b> (<a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <span lang="it" xml:lang="it"><i>Vittorio Emanuele III</i></span>, <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>: <span lang="sq" xml:lang="sq"><i>Viktor Emanueli III</i></span>; 11 November 1869 – 28 December 1947) was the <a href="/wiki/King_of_Italy" title="King of Italy">King of Italy</a> from 29 July 1900 until his <a href="/wiki/Abdication" title="Abdication">abdication</a> on 9 May 1946. In addition, he claimed the thrones of <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Empire" title="Ethiopian Empire">Ethiopia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albanian_Kingdom_(1939%E2%80%931943)" title="Albanian Kingdom (1939–1943)">Albania</a> as <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Ethiopia" title="Emperor of Ethiopia">Emperor of Ethiopia</a> (1936–41) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_the_Albanians" title="King of the Albanians">King of the Albanians</a> (1939–43), claims not recognised by all the <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">great powers</a>. During his long reign (nearly 46 years), which began after the assassination of his father <a href="/wiki/Umberto_I_of_Italy" title="Umberto I of Italy">Umberto I</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a> became involved in two World Wars. His reign also encompassed the birth, rise, and fall of <a href="/wiki/Italian_Fascism" title="Italian Fascism">Italian Fascism</a>.</p>
<p>Victor Emmanuel abdicated his throne in 1946 in favour of his son <a href="/wiki/Umberto_II_of_Italy" title="Umberto II of Italy">Umberto II</a>, hoping to strengthen support for the monarchy against an ultimately successful <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_constitutional_referendum,_1946" title="Italian constitutional referendum, 1946">referendum to abolish it</a>. He then went in exile to <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, where he died and was buried the following year.</p>
<p>He was called by the Italians <i>Il Re soldato</i> (The Soldier King) for having led his country during both the world wars (and for Savoy's historical affinity with the battlefield, where the dynasty built much of its power), and, after Italy's victory in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a> <i>Il Re vittorioso</i> (The Victorious King)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. He was also nicknamed <i>Sciaboletta</i> ("little saber") due to his height of 1.53 m (5 ft 0 in).</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biography">Biography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Biography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queen_Margherita_with_Vittorio_Emanuele.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1234" data-file-width="879" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Queen_Margherita_with_Vittorio_Emanuele.jpg/150px-Queen_Margherita_with_Vittorio_Emanuele.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Queen_Margherita_with_Vittorio_Emanuele.jpg/225px-Queen_Margherita_with_Vittorio_Emanuele.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Queen_Margherita_with_Vittorio_Emanuele.jpg/300px-Queen_Margherita_with_Vittorio_Emanuele.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Queen_Margherita_with_Vittorio_Emanuele.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Young Victor Emmanuel with his mother, <a href="/wiki/Margherita_of_Savoy" title="Margherita of Savoy">Margherita of Savoy</a>, 1876.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Montabone,_Luigi_(18..-1877)_-_Vittorio_Emanuele_III_da_ragazzo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="391" data-file-width="254" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Montabone%2C_Luigi_%2818..-1877%29_-_Vittorio_Emanuele_III_da_ragazzo.jpg/150px-Montabone%2C_Luigi_%2818..-1877%29_-_Vittorio_Emanuele_III_da_ragazzo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Montabone%2C_Luigi_%2818..-1877%29_-_Vittorio_Emanuele_III_da_ragazzo.jpg/225px-Montabone%2C_Luigi_%2818..-1877%29_-_Vittorio_Emanuele_III_da_ragazzo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b1/Montabone%2C_Luigi_%2818..-1877%29_-_Vittorio_Emanuele_III_da_ragazzo.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Montabone,_Luigi_(18..-1877)_-_Vittorio_Emanuele_III_da_ragazzo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Victor Emmanuel as a teenager, 1886.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brogi,_Carlo_(1850-1925)_-_Vittorio_Emanuele_III_di_Savoia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="570" data-file-width="366" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Brogi%2C_Carlo_%281850-1925%29_-_Vittorio_Emanuele_III_di_Savoia.jpg/150px-Brogi%2C_Carlo_%281850-1925%29_-_Vittorio_Emanuele_III_di_Savoia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Brogi%2C_Carlo_%281850-1925%29_-_Vittorio_Emanuele_III_di_Savoia.jpg/225px-Brogi%2C_Carlo_%281850-1925%29_-_Vittorio_Emanuele_III_di_Savoia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Brogi%2C_Carlo_%281850-1925%29_-_Vittorio_Emanuele_III_di_Savoia.jpg/300px-Brogi%2C_Carlo_%281850-1925%29_-_Vittorio_Emanuele_III_di_Savoia.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brogi,_Carlo_(1850-1925)_-_Vittorio_Emanuele_III_di_Savoia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Victor Emmanuel in 1895.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Victor Emmanuel was born in <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Italy</a>. He was the only child of <a href="/wiki/Umberto_I_of_Italy" title="Umberto I of Italy">Umberto I</a>, <a href="/wiki/King_of_Italy" title="King of Italy">King of Italy</a>, and his consort (his first cousin through descent from his grandfather <a href="/wiki/Charles_Albert_of_Sardinia" title="Charles Albert of Sardinia">Charles Albert of Sardinia</a>), <a href="/wiki/Margherita_of_Savoy" title="Margherita of Savoy">Princess Margherita of Savoy</a>. Margherita was the daughter of the Duke of <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Genoa" title="Duke of Genoa">Genoa</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Victor_Emmanuel_III.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="466" data-file-width="281" height="332" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Victor_Emmanuel_III.jpg/200px-Victor_Emmanuel_III.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/db/Victor_Emmanuel_III.jpg 1.5x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Victor_Emmanuel_III.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Victor Emmanuel III by <i><a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(UK_magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (UK magazine)">Vanity Fair</a></i> artist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Libero_Prosperi" title="Libero Prosperi">Libero Prosperi</a>, 1902.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Unlike his paternal first cousin's son, the 1.98 m (6-foot 6") tall <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amedeo,_3rd_Duke_of_Aosta" title="Amedeo, 3rd Duke of Aosta">Amedeo, 3rd Duke of Aosta</a>, Victor Emmanuel was short of stature even by 19th-century standards, to the point that today he would appear diminutive. He was just 1.53 m tall (just over 5 feet).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> From birth until his accession, Victor Emmanuel was known by the title of the <b>Prince of Naples</b>.</p>
<p>On 24 October 1896, Prince Victor Emmanuel married Princess <a href="/wiki/Elena_of_Montenegro" title="Elena of Montenegro">Elena</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Montenegro" title="Kingdom of Montenegro">Montenegro</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accession_to_the_throne">Accession to the throne</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Accession to the throne">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 29 July 1900, at the age of 30, Victor Emmanuel acceded to the throne upon his father's assassination. The only advice that his father Umberto ever gave his heir was "Remember: to be a king, all you need to know is how to sign your name, read a newspaper, and mount a horse".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> His early years showed evidence that, by the standards of the Savoy monarchy, he was a man committed to constitutional government. Indeed, even though his father was killed by an <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchist</a>, the new King showed a commitment to constitutional freedoms.</p>
<p>Though parliamentary rule had been firmly established in Italy, the <a href="/wiki/Statuto_Albertino" title="Statuto Albertino">Statuto Albertino</a>, or constitution, granted the king considerable residual powers. For instance, he had the right to appoint the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Italy" title="Prime Minister of Italy">Prime Minister</a> even if the individual in question did not command majority support in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Chamber_of_Deputies" title="Italian Chamber of Deputies">Chamber of Deputies</a>. A shy and somewhat withdrawn individual, the King hated the day-to-day stresses of Italian politics, though the country's chronic political instability forced him to intervene on no fewer than ten occasions between 1900 and 1922 to solve parliamentary crises.</p>
<p>When <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> began, Italy at first remained neutral, despite being part of the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Alliance_(1882)" title="Triple Alliance (1882)">Triple Alliance</a> (albeit it was signed on defensive terms and Italy objected that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Archduke_Franz_Ferdinand" title="Assassination of Archduke Franz Ferdinand">Sarajevo assassination</a> did not qualify as aggression). However, in 1915, Italy signed several secret treaties committing her to enter the war on the side of the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">Triple Entente</a>. Most of the politicians opposed war, however, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Chamber_of_Deputies" title="Italian Chamber of Deputies">Italian Chamber of Deputies</a> forced Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Salandra" title="Antonio Salandra">Antonio Salandra</a> to resign. At this juncture, Victor Emmanuel declined Salandra's resignation and personally made the decision for Italy to enter the war. He was well within his rights to do so under the <i>Statuto.</i> Popular<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> demonstrations in favor of the war were staged in Rome, with 200,000 gathering on 16 May 1915,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> in the Piazza del Popolo. However, the corrupt and disorganised war effort, the stunning loss of life suffered by the Italian army, especially at the great defeat of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Caporetto" title="Battle of Caporetto">Caporetto</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Post%E2%80%93World_War_I_recession" title="Post–World War I recession">Post–World War I recession</a> turned the King against what he perceived as an inefficient political bourgeoisie. Nevertheless, the King visited the various areas of northern Italy suffering repeated strikes and mortar hits from elements of the fighting there, and demonstrated considerable courage and concern in personally visiting many people, his wife the queen taking turns with nurses in caring for Italy's wounded. It was at this time, the period of World War I, that the King enjoyed the genuine affection of the majority of his people.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Still, during the war he received about 400 threatening letters from people of every social background, mostly working class.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Support_to_Mussolini">Support to Mussolini</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Support to Mussolini">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The economic depression which followed <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> gave rise to much extremism among Italy's sorely tried working classes. This caused the country as a whole to become politically unstable. <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a>, soon to be Italy's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_fascism" title="Italian fascism">Fascist</a> dictator, took advantage of this instability for his rise to power.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="March_on_Rome">March on Rome</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: March on Rome">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_I_and_Victor_Emmanuel_III.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1785" data-file-width="1388" height="257" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Albert_I_and_Victor_Emmanuel_III.jpg/200px-Albert_I_and_Victor_Emmanuel_III.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Albert_I_and_Victor_Emmanuel_III.jpg/300px-Albert_I_and_Victor_Emmanuel_III.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Albert_I_and_Victor_Emmanuel_III.jpg/400px-Albert_I_and_Victor_Emmanuel_III.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albert_I_and_Victor_Emmanuel_III.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
King Victor Emmanuel III (right) with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albert_I_of_the_Belgians" title="Albert I of the Belgians">King Albert I of the Belgians</a> (left). This photograph shows Victor Emmanuel's small physical stature.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1922, Mussolini led a force of his Fascist supporters on a <a href="/wiki/March_on_Rome" title="March on Rome">March on Rome</a>. Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Luigi_Facta" title="Luigi Facta">Luigi Facta</a> and his cabinet drafted a decree of <a href="/wiki/Martial_law" title="Martial law">martial law</a>. After some hesitation the King refused to sign it, citing doubts about the ability of the army to contain the uprising.</p>
<p>Fascist violence had been growing in intensity throughout the summer and autumn of 1922, climaxing in rumours of a possible coup. General <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Badoglio" title="Pietro Badoglio">Pietro Badoglio</a> told the King that the military would be able without difficulty to rout the rebels, who numbered no more than 10,000 men.</p>
<p>The troops were loyal to the King. Even <a href="/wiki/Cesare_Maria_De_Vecchi" title="Cesare Maria De Vecchi">Cesare Maria De Vecchi</a>, commander of the Blackshirts, and one of the organisers of the March on Rome, told Mussolini that he would not act against the wishes of the monarch. It was at this point that the Fascist leader considered leaving Italy altogether. But then, minutes before midnight, he received a telegram from the King inviting him to Rome. By midday on 30 October, he had been appointed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President_of_the_Council_of_Ministers_of_Italy" title="President of the Council of Ministers of Italy">President of the Council of Ministers</a> (Prime Minister), at the age of 39, with no previous experience of office, and with only 35 Fascist deputies in the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_(Italy)" title="Chamber of Deputies (Italy)">Chamber</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Re_darfo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="630" data-file-width="1024" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Re_darfo.jpg/200px-Re_darfo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Re_darfo.jpg/300px-Re_darfo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Re_darfo.jpg/400px-Re_darfo.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Re_darfo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Victor Emmanuel in Darfo Boario Terme after the <a href="/wiki/Gleno_Dam" title="Gleno Dam">Gleno Dam</a> disaster, 1923</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The King failed to move against the Mussolini regime's abuses of power (including, as early as 1924, the assassination of <a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Matteotti" title="Giacomo Matteotti">Giacomo Matteotti</a> and other opposition MPs) and remained silent during the winter of 1925–26 when Mussolini dropped all pretense of democracy. Later that year, Mussolini passed a law declaring that he was responsible to the King, not Parliament. Although under the Statuto Albertino Italian governments were formally answerable only to the monarch, it had been a strong <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_convention_(political_custom)" title="Constitutional convention (political custom)">constitutional convention</a> since at least the 1860s that they were actually answerable to Parliament. By 1928, practically the only check on Mussolini's power was the King's prerogative of dismissing him from office, even if prerogative could only be exercised on the advice of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fascist_Grand_Council" title="Fascist Grand Council">Fascist Grand Council</a>, a body that only Mussolini could convene.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Though the King claimed in his memoirs that it was the fear of a civil war that motivated his actions, it would seem that he received some 'alternative' advice, possibly from the archconservative <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Salandra" title="Antonio Salandra">Antonio Salandra</a> as well as General <a href="/wiki/Armando_Diaz" title="Armando Diaz">Armando Diaz</a>, that it would be better to do a deal with Mussolini.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Whatever the circumstances, Victor Emmanuel showed weakness from a position of strength, with dire future consequences for Italy and for the monarchy itself. Fascism was a force of opposition to left-wing radicalism. This appealed to many people in Italy at the time, and certainly to the King. In many ways, the events from 1922 to 1943 demonstrated that the monarchy and the moneyed class, for different reasons, felt Mussolini and his regime offered an option that, after years of political chaos, was more appealing than what they perceived as the alternative: socialism and <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchism</a>. Both the spectre of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution_of_1917" title="Russian Revolution of 1917">Russian Revolution</a> and the tragedies of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> played a large part in these political decisions. At the same time, the Crown became so closely identified with Fascism that by the time Victor Emmanuel was able to shake himself loose from it, it was too late to save the monarchy.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lateran_Treaty">Lateran Treaty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Lateran Treaty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 1929, Mussolini, on behalf of the King, signed the <a href="/wiki/Lateran_Treaty" title="Lateran Treaty">Lateran Treaty</a>. The treaty was one of the three agreements made that year between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(1861%E2%80%931946)" title="Kingdom of Italy (1861–1946)">Kingdom of Italy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>. On 7 June 1929, the Lateran Treaty was ratified and the "<a href="/wiki/Roman_Question" title="Roman Question">Roman Question</a>" was settled.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Loss_of_popular_support">Loss of popular support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Loss of popular support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eduardo_Gioja_Viktor_Emanuel_III_1913.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3136" data-file-width="2186" height="287" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Eduardo_Gioja_Viktor_Emanuel_III_1913.jpg/200px-Eduardo_Gioja_Viktor_Emanuel_III_1913.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Eduardo_Gioja_Viktor_Emanuel_III_1913.jpg/300px-Eduardo_Gioja_Viktor_Emanuel_III_1913.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Eduardo_Gioja_Viktor_Emanuel_III_1913.jpg/400px-Eduardo_Gioja_Viktor_Emanuel_III_1913.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eduardo_Gioja_Viktor_Emanuel_III_1913.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Victor Emmanuel, 1913 portrait.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Italian monarchy enjoyed popular support for decades.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Foreigners noted how even as late as the 1940s <a href="/wiki/Newsreel" title="Newsreel">newsreel</a> images of King Victor Emmanuel and Queen Elena, born Princess <a href="/wiki/Elena_of_Montenegro" title="Elena of Montenegro">Elena of Montenegro</a>, evoked applause, sometimes cheering, when played in cinemas, in contrast to the hostile silence shown toward images of Fascist leaders.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>On 30 March 1938, the Italian Parliament established the rank of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Marshal_of_the_Empire" title="First Marshal of the Empire">First Marshal of the Empire</a> for Victor Emmanuel and Mussolini. This new rank was the highest rank in the Italian military. His equivalence with Mussolini was seen by the king as offensive and a clear sign, that the ultimate goal of the fascist was to get rid of him.</p>
<p>As popular<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> as Victor Emmanuel was, several of his decisions proved fatal to the monarchy. Among these decisions were his assumption of the imperial crown of <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, his public silence when Mussolini's Fascist government issued its <a href="/wiki/Italian_Racial_Laws" title="Italian Racial Laws">notorious racial purity laws</a>, and his assumption of the crown of <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Emperor_of_Ethiopia">Emperor of Ethiopia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Emperor of Ethiopia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy_and_Horthy_Mikl%C3%B3s_Governor_of_Hungary_at_the_Royal_Castle,_Budapest_%E2%80%93_May,_1937.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3031" data-file-width="4036" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy_and_Horthy_Mikl%C3%B3s_Governor_of_Hungary_at_the_Royal_Castle%2C_Budapest_%E2%80%93_May%2C_1937.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy_and_Horthy_Mikl%C3%B3s_Governor_of_Hungary_at_the_Royal_Castle%2C_Budapest_%E2%80%93_May%2C_1937.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy_and_Horthy_Mikl%C3%B3s_Governor_of_Hungary_at_the_Royal_Castle%2C_Budapest_%E2%80%93_May%2C_1937.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy_and_Horthy_Mikl%C3%B3s_Governor_of_Hungary_at_the_Royal_Castle%2C_Budapest_%E2%80%93_May%2C_1937.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy_and_Horthy_Mikl%C3%B3s_Governor_of_Hungary_at_the_Royal_Castle%2C_Budapest_%E2%80%93_May%2C_1937.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy_and_Horthy_Mikl%C3%B3s_Governor_of_Hungary_at_the_Royal_Castle%2C_Budapest_%E2%80%93_May%2C_1937.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy_and_Horthy_Mikl%C3%B3s_Governor_of_Hungary_at_the_Royal_Castle,_Budapest_%E2%80%93_May,_1937.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Victor Emmanuel III visiting Hungary - 1937</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vittorio_Emanuele_III_1936.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="275" height="291" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Vittorio_Emanuele_III_1936.jpg/200px-Vittorio_Emanuele_III_1936.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/99/Vittorio_Emanuele_III_1936.jpg 1.5x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vittorio_Emanuele_III_1936.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
King Victor Emmanuel III in his uniform as <a href="/wiki/Marshal_of_Italy" title="Marshal of Italy">Marshal of Italy</a> in 1936.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Prior to his government's invasion of <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, Victor Emmanuel travelled in 1934 to <a href="/wiki/Italian_Somaliland" title="Italian Somaliland">Italian Somaliland</a>, where he celebrated his 65th birthday on November 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dsajfsdk_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-dsajfsdk-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bigl7i_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-bigl7i-5">[5]</a></sup> In 1936, Victor Emmanuel assumed the crown as <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Ethiopia" title="Emperor of Ethiopia">Emperor of Ethiopia</a>. His decision to do this was not universally accepted. Victor Emmanuel was only able to assume the crown after the Italian Army invaded Ethiopia (Abyssinia) and overthrew Emperor <a href="/wiki/Haile_Selassie" title="Haile Selassie">Haile Selassie</a> during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Italo-Abyssinian_War" title="Second Italo-Abyssinian War">Second Italo-Abyssinian War</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> condemned Italy's participation in this war and the Italian claim by right of conquest to Ethiopia was rejected by some major powers, such as the United States and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, but was accepted by Great Britain and France in 1938. In 1941 Italy's possession of Ethiopia came to an end only after five years of its annexation to the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Empire" title="Italian Empire">Italian Empire</a>.</p>
<p>The term of the last acting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroy_of_Italian_East_Africa" title="Viceroy of Italian East Africa">Viceroy of Italian East Africa</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Somaliland" title="Italian Somaliland">Italian Somaliland</a>, ended on 27 November 1941 with surrender to the allies. In November 1943 Victor Emmanuel renounced his claims to the titles of Emperor of Ethiopia and King of Albania,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> recognizing the previous holders of those titles as legitimate.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="King_of_the_Albanians">King of the Albanians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: King of the Albanians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The crown of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_the_Albanians" title="King of the Albanians">King of the Albanians</a> had been assumed by Victor Emmanuel in 1939 when Italian forces invaded the nearly defenseless monarchy across the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a> and caused <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zog_of_Albania" title="Zog of Albania">King Zog I</a> to flee. The <a href="/wiki/Italian_invasion_of_Albania" title="Italian invasion of Albania">Italian invasion of Albania</a> was generally seen as the act of a stronger nation taking unfair advantage of a weaker neighbour.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 1941, while in <a href="/wiki/Tirana" title="Tirana">Tirana</a>, the monarch escaped an assassination attempt by the 19-year-old Albanian patriot <a href="/wiki/Vasil_La%C3%A7i" title="Vasil Laçi">Vasil Laçi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pearson153_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pearson153-7">[7]</a></sup> Later, this attempt was cited by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist_Albania" title="Communist Albania">Communist Albania</a> as a sign of the general discontent among the oppressed Albanian population. A second attempt by Dimitri Mikhaliov in Albania gave the Italians an excuse to affirm a possible connection with <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> as a result of the monarch's assent to the <a href="/wiki/Greco-Italian_War" title="Greco-Italian War">Greco-Italian War</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VE3_lira_1940.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="732" data-file-width="1438" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/VE3_lira_1940.jpg/250px-VE3_lira_1940.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/VE3_lira_1940.jpg/375px-VE3_lira_1940.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/VE3_lira_1940.jpg/500px-VE3_lira_1940.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VE3_lira_1940.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Image of Victor Emmanuel on a 1941 <a href="/wiki/Lira" title="Lira">lira</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_efforts_to_save_crown">Final efforts to save crown</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Final efforts to save crown">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 10 June 1940, ignoring advice that the country was unprepared, Mussolini made the fatal decision to have Italy enter <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> on the side of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>. Almost from the beginning, disaster followed disaster. In 1940 Italian armies in North Africa and in Greece suffered humiliating defeats. During the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Yugoslavia" title="Invasion of Yugoslavia">invasion of Yugoslavia</a> in April 1941, Victor Emmanuel moved to a villa owned by the Pirzio Biroli family at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazzacco" title="Brazzacco">Brazzacco</a> in order to be close to the front.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> In late 1941, <a href="/wiki/Italian_East_Africa" title="Italian East Africa">Italian East Africa</a> was lost. In 1942, <a href="/wiki/Italian_Libya" title="Italian Libya">Italian Libya</a> was lost. Early in 1943, the ten divisions of the "<a href="/wiki/Italian_Army_in_Russia" title="Italian Army in Russia">Italian Army in Russia</a>" (<i>Armata Italiana in Russia</i>, or ARMIR) were crushed in a side-action the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad" title="Battle of Stalingrad">Battle of Stalingrad</a>. Before the end of 1943, the last Italian forces in <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a> had surrendered and <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> had been taken by the Allies. Hampered by lack of fuel as well as several serious defeats, the Italian Navy spent most of the war confined to port. As a result the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> was not in any real sense Italy's <i><a href="/wiki/Mare_Nostrum" title="Mare Nostrum">Mare Nostrum</a></i>. While the Air Force generally did better than the Army or the Navy, it was chronically short of modern aircraft and had limitations sufficiently evident for it to be excluded by Italy's allies from a part in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain" title="Battle of Britain">Battle of Britain</a>.</p>
<p>As Italy's fortunes worsened, the popularity of the King suffered. One coffee-house ditty went as follows:</p>
<dl>
<dd><i>Quando Vittorio era soltanto re</i></dd>
<dd><i>Si bevea del buon caffè.</i></dd>
<dd><i>Poi divenne Imperatore</i></dd>
<dd><i>Se ne sentì solo l’odore.</i></dd>
<dd><i>Oggi che è anche Re d’Albania</i></dd>
<dd><i>Anche l’odore l’ han portato via.</i></dd>
<dd><i>E se avremo un’altra vittoria</i></dd>
<dd><i>Ci mancherà anche la cicoria.</i></dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dd>"When our Victor was plain King,</dd>
<dd>Coffee was a common thing.</dd>
<dd>When an Emperor he was made,</dd>
<dd>Coffee's odour it did fade.</dd>
<dd>Since he got Albania's throne,</dd>
<dd>Even the odour has flown.</dd>
<dd>And if we have another victory</dd>
<dd>We're also going to lose our <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chicory_Root_Extract" title="Chicory Root Extract">chicory</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Little_King_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Little_King-9">[9]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<p>On 19 July 1943, Rome was <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Rome_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Rome in World War II">bombed for the first time</a> in the war, further cementing the Italian people's disillusionment with their once-popular<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> King.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Coup_d.27.C3.A9tat_against_Mussolini">Coup d'état against Mussolini</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Coup d'état against Mussolini">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/25_Luglio" title="25 Luglio">25 Luglio</a></div>
<p>On the night of 25 July 1943, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Council_of_Fascism" title="Grand Council of Fascism">Grand Council of Fascism</a> voted to adopt an <i>Ordine del Giorno</i> (order of the day) proposed by Count <a href="/wiki/Dino_Grandi" title="Dino Grandi">Dino Grandi</a> to ask Victor Emmanuel to resume his full constitutional powers under Article 5 of the <i>Statuto.</i> In effect, this was a <a href="/wiki/Motion_of_no_confidence" title="Motion of no confidence">motion of no confidence</a> in Mussolini.</p>
<p>The following afternoon, Mussolini asked for an audience with the king at Villa Savoia. When Mussolini tried to tell Victor Emmanuel about the Grand Council's vote, Victor Emmanuel abruptly cut him off and told him that he was dismissing him as Prime Minister in favour of <a href="/wiki/Marshal" title="Marshal">Marshal</a> <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Badoglio" title="Pietro Badoglio">Pietro Badoglio</a>. He then ordered Mussolini's arrest and he proceeded to renounce the usurped Ethiopian and Albanian crowns in favour of the legitimate monarchs of those states. Victor Emmanuel had been planning this move to get rid of the dictator for some time.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Publicly, Victor Emmanuel and Badoglio claimed that Italy would continue the war as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis</a>. Privately, they both began negotiating with the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a> for an armistice. Court circles—including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marie-Jos%C3%A9_of_Belgium" title="Marie-José of Belgium">Crown Princess Marie-José</a>—had already been putting out feelers to the Allies before Mussolini's ousting.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Armistice_with_the_Allies">Armistice with the Allies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Armistice with the Allies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 8 September 1943, Victor Emmanuel publicly announced an <a href="/wiki/Armistice_of_Cassibile" title="Armistice of Cassibile">armistice with the Allies</a>. Confusion reigned as Italian forces were left without orders, and the Germans, who had been expecting this move for some time, quickly disarmed and interned Italian troops and took control in the occupied Balkans, France and the <a href="/wiki/Dodecanese" title="Dodecanese">Dodecanese</a>, as well as in Italy itself. Many of the units that did not surrender joined forces with the Allies against the Germans.</p>
<p>Fearing a German advance on Rome, Victor Emmanuel and his government fled south to <a href="/wiki/Brindisi" title="Brindisi">Brindisi</a>. This choice may have been necessary to protect his safety; indeed, Hitler had planned to arrest him shortly after Mussolini's overthrow. Nonetheless, it still came as a surprise to many observers inside and outside Italy. Unfavourable comparisons were drawn with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_VI_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George VI of the United Kingdom">King George VI</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Bowes-Lyon" title="Elizabeth Bowes-Lyon">Queen Elizabeth</a>, who refused to leave London during <a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">the Blitz</a>, and of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XII" title="Pope Pius XII">Pope Pius XII</a>, who mixed with Rome's crowds and prayed with them after Rome's working-class neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Quartiere_San_Lorenzo" title="Quartiere San Lorenzo">Quartiere San Lorenzo</a> had been destroyed by bombing.</p>
<p>Ultimately, the Badoglio regime in southern Italy raised the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Co-Belligerent_Army" title="Italian Co-Belligerent Army">Italian Co-Belligerent Army</a> (<i>Esercito Cobelligerante del Sud</i>), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Co-Belligerent_Air_Force" title="Italian Co-Belligerent Air Force">Italian Co-Belligerent Air Force</a> (<i>Aviazione Cobelligerante Italiana</i>), and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Co-Belligerent_Navy" title="Italian Co-Belligerent Navy">Italian Co-Belligerent Navy</a> (<i>Marina Cobelligerante del Sud</i>). All three forces were loyal to the King.</p>
<p>On 12 September, the Germans launched <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Eiche" title="Operation Eiche">Operation Eiche</a> and rescued Mussolini from captivity. In a short time, he established a new Fascist state in northern Italy, the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Social_Republic" title="Italian Social Republic">Italian Social Republic</a> (<i>Repubblica Sociale Italiana</i>). This was never more than a Nazi-dominated <a href="/wiki/Puppet_state" title="Puppet state">puppet state</a>, but it did compete for the allegiance of the Italian people with Badoglio's Allied-controlled government in the south.</p>
<p>Realizing that he was too tainted by his earlier support of the Fascist regime, in April 1944 Victor Emmanuel transferred most of his powers to his son, <a href="/wiki/Umberto_II_of_Italy" title="Umberto II of Italy">Crown Prince Umberto</a>. By so doing, Emmanuel relinquished most of his power while retaining the title of king. This status was formalized shortly after Rome was liberated on 4 June, when he turned over his remaining powers to Umberto and named him <a href="/wiki/Luogotenente" title="Luogotenente">Lieutenant General of the Realm</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1946_referendum">1946 referendum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 1946 referendum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Within a year, public opinion forced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_constitutional_referendum,_1946" title="Italian constitutional referendum, 1946">a referendum</a> on whether to retain the monarchy or become a republic. On 9 May 1946, hoping to win over voters to the monarchist cause, Victor Emmanuel formally abdicated, and was succeeded by son Umberto II. This move failed. In the referendum held a month later, 52 percent of voters favoured a republic, and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a> was no more. Some historians (such as Sir <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_Petrie_(historian)" title="Charles Petrie (historian)">Charles Petrie</a>) have speculated that the result might have been different if Victor Emmanuel had abdicated in favour of Umberto shortly after the Allied invasion of Sicily in 1943, or at the latest had abdicated outright in 1944 rather than simply transferring his powers to his son. Umberto had been widely praised for his performance as <i>de facto</i> head of state beginning in 1944, and his relative popularity might have saved the monarchy. The Italian conductor <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Toscanini" title="Arturo Toscanini">Arturo Toscanini</a> declared that he would not come back to Italy as a subject of the "degenerate king" and more generally as long as the house of Savoy was ruling;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Benedetto_Croce" title="Benedetto Croce">Benedetto Croce</a> had previously stated in 1944 that "as long as the present king remains head of state, we feel that Fascism has not ended, (...) that it will be reborn, more or less disguised".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>In any event, once the referendum's result was officialized, all male members of the House of Savoy were required to leave the country, never to return.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Taking refuge in <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Egypt" title="Kingdom of Egypt">Egypt</a>, Victor Emmanuel died in <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a> the following year, and was buried there, behind the altar of <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Alexandria" title="Catherine of Alexandria">St Catherine's Cathedral</a>. He was the last surviving grandchild of <a href="/wiki/Victor_Emmanuel_II_of_Italy" title="Victor Emmanuel II of Italy">Victor Emmanuel II of Italy</a>. In 1948, <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine included an article about "The Little King".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Little_King_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_Little_King-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Remo023.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1952" data-file-width="2592" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/San_Remo023.jpg/250px-San_Remo023.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/San_Remo023.jpg/375px-San_Remo023.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/San_Remo023.jpg/500px-San_Remo023.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_Remo023.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Busts of King Victor Emmanuel III and Queen Elena; forecourt of the Russian Orthodox Church (Church of Christ the Saviour, St. Catherine and St. Seraph). Sanremo, Italy</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The abdication prior to the referendum probably brought back to the minds of undecided voters the monarchy's role during the Fascist period and the King's own actions (or lack of them), at the very moment monarchists hoped voters would focus on the positive impression created by Umberto and his wife, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marie-Jos%C3%A9_of_Belgium" title="Marie-José of Belgium">Princess Maria José</a> over the previous two years. The 'May' King and Queen, Umberto and Maria José, in Umberto's brief, month-long reign, were unable to shift the burden of recent history and opinion.</p>
<p>Victor Emmanuel III was one of the most prolific <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coin_collectors" title="Coin collectors">coin collectors</a> of all time, having amassed approximately 100,000 specimens dating from the fall of the Roman Empire up to the Unification of Italy. On his abdication, the collection was donated to the Italian people, except for the coins of the House of Savoy which he took with him to Egypt. On the death of <a href="/wiki/Umberto_II_of_Italy" title="Umberto II of Italy">Umberto II</a> in 1983, the Savoy coins joined the rest of the collection in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Museo_Nazionale_Romano" title="Museo Nazionale Romano">National Museum of Rome</a>. Between 1910 and 1943 Victor Emmanuel wrote the 20-volume <i>Corpus Nummorum Italicorum,</i> which catalogued each specimen in his collection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> He was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Medal_of_the_Royal_Numismatic_Society" title="Medal of the Royal Numismatic Society">medal of the Royal Numismatic Society</a> in 1904.</p>
<p>At one point there was an avenue in Paris named <i>Avenue Victor-Emmanuel III,</i> but the fascist king's support of the Axis Powers led the road to be renamed <i>Franklin D. Roosevelt Avenue</i> following the end of World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles_of_the_Crown_of_Italy">Titles of the Crown of Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Titles of the Crown of Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CoA_Victor_Emmanuele_III_Italia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4147" data-file-width="2897" height="315" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/CoA_Victor_Emmanuele_III_Italia.jpg/220px-CoA_Victor_Emmanuele_III_Italia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/CoA_Victor_Emmanuele_III_Italia.jpg/330px-CoA_Victor_Emmanuele_III_Italia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/CoA_Victor_Emmanuele_III_Italia.jpg/440px-CoA_Victor_Emmanuele_III_Italia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CoA_Victor_Emmanuele_III_Italia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Relief of coat of arms of Victor Emmanuel III in Rhodes, Greece</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From 1860 to 1946, the following titles were used by the <a href="/wiki/King_of_Italy" title="King of Italy">King of Italy</a>:</p>
<p>Victor Emmanuel III, <a href="/wiki/By_the_Grace_of_God" title="By the Grace of God">by the Grace of God</a> and the Will of the Nation, <a href="/wiki/King_of_Italy" title="King of Italy">King of Italy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_Sardinia" title="King of Sardinia">King of Sardinia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Cyprus" title="Kingdom of Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kings_of_Jerusalem" title="Kings of Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Kingdom_of_Cilicia" title="Armenian Kingdom of Cilicia">Armenia</a>, Duke of Savoy, <a href="/wiki/Count" title="Count">count</a> of <a href="/wiki/Maurienne" title="Maurienne">Maurienne</a>, Marquis (of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>) in Italy; Prince of <a href="/wiki/Piedmont" title="Piedmont">Piedmont</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carignano" title="Carignano">Carignano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oneglia" title="Oneglia">Oneglia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poirino" title="Poirino">Poirino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trino" title="Trino">Trino</a>; Prince and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Perpetual_vicar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Perpetual vicar (page does not exist)">Perpetual vicar</a> of the Holy Roman Empire; prince of <a href="/wiki/Carmagnola" title="Carmagnola">Carmagnola</a>, Montmellian with Arbin and Francin, prince <a href="/wiki/Bailiff" title="Bailiff">bailliff</a> of the Duchy of <a href="/wiki/Aosta" title="Aosta">Aosta</a>, Prince of <a href="/wiki/Chieri" title="Chieri">Chieri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dronero" title="Dronero">Dronero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crescentino" title="Crescentino">Crescentino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riva_presso_Chieri" title="Riva presso Chieri">Riva di Chieri</a> and Banna, <a href="/wiki/Busca" title="Busca">Busca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bene_Vagienna" title="Bene Vagienna">Bene</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bra,_Italy" title="Bra, Italy">Brà</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Genoa" title="Duke of Genoa">Duke of Genoa</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rulers_of_Montferrat" title="Rulers of Montferrat">Monferrat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aosta" title="Aosta">Aosta</a>, Duke of <a href="/wiki/Chablais" title="Chablais">Chablais</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genevois_(province)" title="Genevois (province)">Genevois</a>, Duke of <a href="/wiki/Piacenza" title="Piacenza">Piacenza</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marquis" title="Marquis">Marquis</a> of <a href="/wiki/Saluzzo" title="Saluzzo">Saluzzo</a> (Saluces), <a href="/wiki/Ivrea" title="Ivrea">Ivrea</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Susa_(Italy)" title="Susa (Italy)">Susa</a>, of Maro, <a href="/wiki/Oristano" title="Oristano">Oristano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cesana_Torinese" title="Cesana Torinese">Cesana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Savona" title="Savona">Savona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mo%C3%BBtiers" title="Moûtiers">Tarantasia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borgomanero" title="Borgomanero">Borgomanero</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cureggio" title="Cureggio">Cureggio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caselle_Torinese" title="Caselle Torinese">Caselle</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rivoli_(TO)" title="Rivoli (TO)">Rivoli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pianezza" title="Pianezza">Pianezza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Govone" title="Govone">Govone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salussola" title="Salussola">Salussola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racconigi" title="Racconigi">Racconigi</a> with Tegerone, Migliabruna and Motturone, <a href="/wiki/Cavallermaggiore" title="Cavallermaggiore">Cavallermaggiore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marene" title="Marene">Marene</a>, <a href="/wiki/Modane" title="Modane">Modane</a> and <a <a href="/wiki/Vercelli" title="Vercelli">Vercelli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pinerolo" title="Pinerolo">Pinerolo</a>, of <a href="/wiki/Lomellina" title="Lomellina">Lomellina</a>, of <a title="Patrician (post-Roman Europe)">patrician</a> of <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>, patrician of <a href="/wiki/Ferrara" title="Ferrara">Ferrara</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Family">Family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BASA-3K-15-637-1-Giovanna_of_Italy,_1937.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2344" data-file-width="1968" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/BASA-3K-15-637-1-Giovanna_of_Italy%2C_1937.jpeg/200px-BASA-3K-15-637-1-Giovanna_of_Italy%2C_1937.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/BASA-3K-15-637-1-Giovanna_of_Italy%2C_1937.jpeg/300px-BASA-3K-15-637-1-Giovanna_of_Italy%2C_1937.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/BASA-3K-15-637-1-Giovanna_of_Italy%2C_1937.jpeg/400px-BASA-3K-15-637-1-Giovanna_of_Italy%2C_1937.jpeg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BASA-3K-15-637-1-Giovanna_of_Italy,_1937.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Giovanna of Italy, Tsaritsa of Bulgaria, 1937.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1896 he married princess <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jelena_of_Montenegro" title="Jelena of Montenegro">Elena of Montenegro</a> (1873–1952), daughter of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nicholas_I_of_Montenegro" title="Nicholas I of Montenegro">Nicholas I</a>, King of <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>. Their issue included:</p>
<ol>
<li><a href="/wiki/Princess_Yolanda_of_Savoy" title="Princess Yolanda of Savoy">Yolanda Margherita Milena Elisabetta Romana Maria</a> (1901–1986), married to Giorgio Carlo Calvi, Count of <a href="/wiki/Bergolo" title="Bergolo">Bergolo</a>, (1887–1977);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Princess_Mafalda_of_Savoy" title="Princess Mafalda of Savoy">Mafalda Maria Elisabetta Anna Romana</a> (1902–1944), married to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Philipp_of_Hesse" title="Prince Philipp of Hesse">Prince Philipp of Hesse</a> (1896–1980) with issue; she died in the <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazi</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Concentration_camp" title="Concentration camp">concentration camp</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buchenwald" title="Buchenwald">Buchenwald</a>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Umberto_II_of_Italy" title="Umberto II of Italy">Umberto Nicola Tommaso Giovanni Maria</a>, later Umberto II, King of Italy (1904–1983) married to Princess <a href="/wiki/Marie_Jos%C3%A9_of_Belgium" title="Marie José of Belgium">Marie José of Belgium</a> (1906–2001), with issue.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Giovanna_of_Italy" title="Giovanna of Italy">Giovanna Elisabetta Antonia Romana Maria</a> (1907–2000), married to King <a href="/wiki/Boris_III_of_Bulgaria" title="Boris III of Bulgaria">Boris III</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> (1894–1943), and mother of <a href="/wiki/Simeon_Saxe-Coburg-Gotha" title="Simeon Saxe-Coburg-Gotha">Simeon II</a>, King and later <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Bulgaria" title="Prime Minister of Bulgaria">Prime Minister of Bulgaria</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Princess_Maria_Francesca_of_Savoy" title="Princess Maria Francesca of Savoy">Maria Francesca Anna Romana</a> (1914–2001), who married Prince Luigi of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bourbon%E2%80%93Parma" title="Bourbon–Parma">Bourbon–Parma</a> (1899–1967), with issue.</li>
</ol>
